PlanGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder implementation that builds a graph for\n19: // planning and for other \"plan-like\" operations which don't require an\n20: // already-calculated plan as input.\n21: //\n22: // Unlike the apply graph builder, this graph builder:\n23: //\n24: //   - Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which\n25: //     represents the desired state.\n26: //\n27: //   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because\n28: //     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning\n29: //     to take against a \t// of the plan walk.\n40: \tRootVariableValues InputValues\n41: \n42: \t// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider\n43: \t// configurations that the graph builder should generated a NoOp or Update action then we'll force generating a replace\n57: \t// action instead. Create and Delete actions are not affected.\n58: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n59: \n60: \t// skipRefresh indicates that we should skip refreshing managed resources\n61: \tskipRefresh bool\n62: \n63: \t// preDestroyRefresh indicates that we are executing the refresh which\n64: \t// happens immediately before a destroy plan, which happens to use the\n65: \t// normal planing mode so skipPlanChanges cannot be set.\n66: \tpreDestroyRefresh bool\n67: \n68: \t// skipPlanChanges indicates that we should skip the step of comparing\n69: \t// prior state with configuration and generating planned changes to\n70: \t// resource instances. (This is for the \"refresh only\" planning mode,\n71: \t// where we _only_ do the refresh step.)\n72: \tskipPlanChanges bool\n73: \n74: \tConcreteProvider                ConcreteProviderNodeFunc\n75: ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n78: \tConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposedNodeFunc\n79: \tConcreteModule                  ConcreteModuleNodeFunc\n80: \n81: \t// Plan Operation this graph will be used for.\n82: \tOperation walkOperation\n83: \n84: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n85: \t// nodes that should not be pruned This must be provided by the Context\n69: // initializer.\n70: type ContextMeta struct {\n71: \tEnv string // Env is the state environment\n72: \n73: \t// OriginalWorkingDir is the working directory where the Terraform CLI\n74: \t// was run from, which may no longer actually be the current working\n75: \t// directory if the user included the -chdir=... option.\n76: \t//\n77: \t// If this string is empty then the original working directory is the same\n78: \t// as the current working directory.\n79: \t//\n80: \t// In most cases we should respect the user's override by ignoring this\n81: \t// path and just using the current working directory, but this is here\n82: \t// for some exceptional cases where the original working directory is\n83: \t// needed.\n84: \tOriginalWorkingDir string\n85: }\n86: \n87: // Context represents all the context that Terraform needs in order to\n88: // perform operations on infrastructure. This structure is built using\n89: // NewContext.\n90: type Context struct {\n91: \t// meta captures some misc. information about the working directory where\n92: \t// we're taking these actions, and thus which should remain steady between\n93: \t// operations.\n94: \tmeta *ContextMeta\n95: \n96: \tplugins *contextPlugins\n97: \n98: \thooks   []Hook\n99: \tsh      *stopHook\n100: \tuiInput UIInput\n101: \n102: \tl                   sync.Mutex // Lock acquired during any task\n103: \tparallelSem         Semaphore\n104: \tproviderInputConfig map[string]map[string]cty.Value\n105: \trunCond             *sync.Cond\n106: \trunContext          context.Context\n107: \trunContextCancel    context.CancelFunc\n108: }\n109: \n110: // (additional methods on Context can be found in context_*.go files.)\n111: \n112: // NewContext creates a new Context structure.\n113: //\n114: // Once a Context is created, the caller must not access or mutate any of\n115: // the objects referenced (directly or indirectly) by the ContextOpts fields.\n116: //\n117: // If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the resulting context is\n118: // invalid and must not be used.\n119: func NewContext(opts *ContextOpts) (*Context, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n120: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n121: \n122: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] terraform.NewContext: starting\")\n123: \n124: \t// Copy all the hooks and add our stop hook. We don't append directly\n125: \t// to the Config so that we're not modifying that in-place.\n126: \tsh := new(stopHook)\n127: \thooks := make([]Hook, len(opts.Hooks)+1)\n128: \tcopy(hooks, opts.Hooks)\n129: \thooks[len(opts.Hooks)] = sh\n130: \n131: \t// Determine parallelism, default to 10. We do this both to limit\n132: \t// CPU pressure but also to have an extra guard against rate throttling\n133: \t// from providers.\n134: \t// We throw an error in case of negative parallelism\n135: \tpar := opts.Parallelism\n136: \tif par < 0 {\n137: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n138: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n139: \t\t\t\"Invalid parallelism value\",\n140: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The parallelism must be a positive value. Not %d.\", par),\n141: \t\t))\n142: \t\treturn nil, diags\n143: \t}\n144: \n145: \tif par == 0 {\n146: \t\tpar = 10\n147: \t}\n148: \n149: \tplugins := newContextPlugins(opts.Providers, opts.Provisioners, opts.PreloadedProviderSchemas)\n150: \n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/internal/terraform/context.go%3FL1-150"}}}

Current resource instance objects from prior state\n  - Current deposed objects (previous generation of instances marked for destruction)\n  - Ephemeral values from state\n- Enables nodes to compare desired state (config) with current state during evaluation\n\n### Additional Key Transformers in Sequence\n1. **AttachResourceConfigTransformer** (line 215): Attaches config blocks to resource nodes\n2. **ModuleExpansionTransformer** (line 230): Creates nodes for module calls and expansion\n3. **AttachSchemaTransformer** (line 225): Attaches provider schemas for type checking\n4. **DestroyEdgeTransformer** (line 247): Creates destroy edges for resource dependencies\n5. **TargetsTransformer** (line 256): Filters graph to only include targeted resources\n6. **CloseProviderTransformer** (line 266): Creates nodes to close provider connections\n\n### Graph Building Flow\n1. Config nodes created with resource/data source/module instances\n2. Root variables and module variables injected\n3. State from prior run attached\n4.
